13/12/2024, 18:40 - Alex: Your situation seems to involve a misunderstanding or mishandling of the payment process and notification timing. Here's a breakdown:

### What Likely Happened:
1. **November 2, 2023:**
   - You received a notification from Autovia indicating an **administrative fee of ‚Ç¨60** for processing the fine on your behalf, as per their rental terms.
   - Autovia withdrew **‚Ç¨60** from your account. However, this amount was **only for their administrative fee** and did **not cover the traffic fine itself**. The traffic fine was never paid to the Municipality of Florence.

2. **December 13, 2024:**
   - You received the formal notification of the traffic fine from the Municipality of Florence, over a year after the violation and well past the reduced payment period.
   - The Municipality is now demanding the **full fine amount (‚Ç¨180)** because their system considers the deadlines for reduced payments as expired.

### Key Issue:
The **delayed notification to you** is problematic. Under Italian law (**Art. 201 of the Traffic Code**), traffic fines must be notified to the driver:
   - **Within 360 days** from the date the rental company provided your details to the authorities.

   In your case, Autovia provided your details on **October 26, 2023**, meaning the Municipality had until **October 20, 2024**, to notify you. Receiving the fine notification on **December 13, 2024**, exceeds this legal timeframe.

### What You Can Do:
1. **Challenge the Fine Based on Late Notification**:
   - You have grounds to dispute the fine because the notification arrived more than 360 days after Autovia provided your details. This violates Italian traffic fine notification rules.
   - File an appeal with the **Prefect of Florence** or the **Justice of the Peace**.
     - **Prefect Appeal**: Free, but if rejected, the fine doubles.
     - **Justice of the Peace Appeal**: May involve a small fee but has a better chance of success.

2. **Evidence to Support Your Case**:
   - Show that you received the fine notification on **December 13, 2024**, which is beyond the legal notification deadline.
   - Provide proof of the ‚Ç¨60 payment to Autovia and clarify that you believed this covered the fine.

3. **Steps to Appeal**:
   - Appeals must be written in **Italian**.
   - Include:
     - Your personal details and address.
     - Fine reference number (**Z/5221520/2023**).
     - Explanation of late notification and your payment history.
   - Submit to:
     - **Prefect of Florence**: Corpo Polizia Municipale di Firenze ‚Äì Ufficio Ricorsi ‚Äì Via delle Cascine n.9, 50144 Firenze.
     - **Justice of the Peace**: Palazzo di Giustizia - Viale Alessandro Guidoni 61, 50127 Firenze.

4. **Immediate Action**:
   - Contact **Safety21 S.p.A.** or the Municipality of Florence to explain the situation and confirm if they recognize the late notification. They may rectify the issue without requiring an appeal.

   - **Contact Details**:
     - Email: **firenze@myfines.it**
     - Phone: **+39-0763-616514**.

### Summary:
- The fine's notification appears **illegally delayed**. You should not be liable for the full ‚Ç¨180 fine due to this delay.
- The **‚Ç¨60 you paid** was for Autovia's administrative processing, not the fine.
- You have a strong basis for an appeal. Let me know if you'd like help drafting the necessary documents or reaching out to the authorities.
